I'm a 64 y/o Harley rider. My wife was shopping around town. I went in to an empty bar, walked in waved to the young man on  the outdoor smoking patio. He turned out to be the bartender. I made some small talk and joined he and friends outside (smokers). They all were very welcoming. Asked if there was anywhere in the shade,  they said hey park right here next to the glass block wall. I drank up said I may see you at the live music later. < review>
Peri's Silver Dollar bar is a bar and entertainment venue in Fairfax. One of the two main music venues in town and both are institutions. Fairfax has a long history of good musicians and local bands. Just tonight two 'guest performers' dropped in and played and /or sang with the scheduled band on the 'patio' which is an outdoor room without windows. Uniquely Fairfax. The 'patio' band starts around 5.00pm and plays till around 8:00pm. No food served here and it is on a cash only basis. There is an outside area in back where locals relax and play ping-pong until the main band starts up at 9:00pm.
The music is good and you don't get shorted on the drinks. If you enjoy music, Peri's is good.<//review>

I love the food here so much that if I am in the area between 11 and 2:00 pm I will place a takeout order and grab it on my way back to Ventura. When the bill came I was charged twenty eight dollars. I thought wow tax has really gone up in Los Angeles county! After walking back to my car I rechecked the online menu again and called the restaurant regarding being overcharged by nine dollars. <Text>Fantastic fish, highest quality sushi prepared by a true master chef.  Not sure why these people give it low ratings, most likely they are used to mayonnaise roll style bars that chop up and mince inferior quality fish, or prefer non-traditional style sushi that is nothing but rolls rolls rolls with crunchy tidbits on top, because this place is the bomb. The owner takes great care to serve the best fish, in correct order, in correct portions.  He will guide you as to what to use soy sauce on, what not too.  This place is as good as any omakase resaurant on the Westside, and a hidden gem.  Those of you that know good sushi will love this place. After eating lunch near the Oceanside pier, we went looking for ice cream. Instead of ice cream we found this bakery, and are we glad we did. <date>1549852987356</date><text>I don‚Äôt often order an omelette. For me, that‚Äôs usually only the safe choice when I can‚Äôt find anything truly appealing. 99% of omelets are scrambled eggs with mediocre ingredients. But for some reason, I was intrigued by the offering at Petite Madeline.

First off, to set the stage, I was ravenous after just completing a long run. Sunday morning post-run breakfast for me is more like an attack by a wild animal than typical human dining. So apologies to the staff if I left a mess ;)

The omelette arrived and immediately it appeared different than what I‚Äôm used to. The egg was delicately folded - more like the dough of a croissant than the typical globular mess of most omelettes. There was a generous portion of the ingredients atop the whole thing and more within. The sausage was absolutely perfect. Full flavored and moist but not the typical acrid assault on the taste buds from cheap breakfast sausage. The goat cheese was perfectly tart and prolifically distributed. Add in spinach and onions, and this was one delightfully flavorful (and filling) meal.

The coffee was also excellent. My girlfriend had a delicious oatmeal bowl that I envied in silence.

Why 4 and not 5 stars? I reserve 5 stars for mind blowing experiences. This was very good and highly recommended. But it‚Äôs not in my top three favorite breakfast places, and I have to draw the line somewhere.</text><Response>None</Response>< pics>

< Text>
This is a cozy little spot in the downtown area of Oceanside. We came here because the place across the street was super busy. For a small little bakery, they were able to accommodate 10 of us in under 10 minutes. Grant it, we were a little tight and really close to our neighboring table, but we were starving so we didn't mind.

The staff here is super friendly and served us very quickly. I ordered a "Mocha de Mexico w/peanuts" which tasted like a hot chocolate with a hint of a peanut flavor. It was decent, but I wish it would have came served a little hotter. The temperature wasn't very hot. I also ordered their two egg breakfast, with wheat toast and homefried potatoes. Their potatoes were delicious! The rest of the breakfast was good too, but the crepes were the hit at the table.

I'm glad we diverted from the place across the street and came here. We were very satisfied with the service and tasty food made from scratch!

(Breakfast served from 7am-3pm)<//Text>

< text>
I have come here several times for coffee and a pastry to go. Their coffee is good, they have lots of variety of baked goods and their prices are reasonable. For mother's day, all I wanted to do was finally go here for breakfast and it was such a disappointment. We had to pay for our food and tip before we got any food or service which was different but I tipped 18% assuming their service would be as good as their coffee. Food came relatively fast but they didn't make my husband's pancakes so we had to wait close to 10 minutes for those and my omlette had ham instead of sausage. Not to mention, my entire plate had a THICK layer of oil. My home fries weren't great and I choked through half my omlette that was literally dripping with oil because I had already paid $65 for our food and didn't want to waste it. My husband just got pancakes, hashbrowns and bacon and his was somehow covered in oil too. We are now home and both have stomach aches and regret. Service was dumpy to say the least. I never got a refill on my coffee and had to flag down people for our forgotten food. We were checked on once as we were about to leave but didn't have a set server, it was kinda whoever was around I guess. So sad because I loved this place as a nice coffee stop but I'm never going back.</text>
